Publisher's Summary
2019 was the last great year for the world economy.

For generations, everything has been getting faster, better, and cheaper. Finally, we reached the point that almost anything you could ever want could be sent to your home within daysâeven hoursâof when you decided you wanted it.

America made that happen, but now America has lost interest in keeping it going.

Globe-spanning supply chains are only possible with the protection of the U.S. Navy. The American dollar underpins internationalized energy and financial markets. Complex, innovative industries were created to satisfy American consumers. American security policy forced warring nations to lay down their arms. Billions of people have been fed and educated as the American-led trade system spread across the globe.

All of this was artificial. All this was temporary. All this is ending.

In The End of the World Is Just the Beginning, author and geopolitical strategist Peter Zeihan maps out the next world: a world where countries or regions will have no choice but to make their own goods, grow their own food, secure their own energy, fight their own battles, and do it all with populations that are both shrinking and aging.

The list of countries that make it all work is smaller than you think. Which means everything about our interconnected worldâfrom how we manufacture products, to how we grow food, to how we keep the lights on, to how we shuttle stuff about, to how we pay for it allâis about to change.

A world ending. A world beginning. Zeihan brings listeners along for an illuminating (and a bit terrifying) ride packed with foresight, wit, and his trademark irreverence.1 / 1ChatGPT"The End of the World Is Just the Beginning" by Peter Zeihan examines the imminent collapse of globalization. The book argues that the prosperity and interconnectedness the world experienced, driven by America's influence in establishing global supply chains, international financial markets, and security, was temporary and is now ending. The U.S. played a pivotal role in this system, but its interest in maintaining it has waned. As globalization breaks down, countries will need to become self-sufficient in areas like manufacturing, agriculture, and energy. Many countries may struggle in this new reality, especially given challenges like aging and shrinking populations. Zeihan offers a perspective that is both enlightening and unsettling, emphasizing the dramatic shifts the world is about to undergo.1 / 1The End of the World Is Just the Beginning: Mapping the Collapse of Globalization is a nonfiction book written by Peter Zeihan, a geopolitical strategist who formerly worked for the geopolitical intelligence firm Stratfor. The book was published by Harper Business in June 2022.

Background
Edit
What is currently referred to as deglobalization has been the focus of much of the author's research since 2012, when he left Stratfor and founded his own consulting firm.


Summary
Edit
This book's analysis covers six different economic sectors:

Agriculture
Energy
Finance
Manufacturing
Materials
Transport
Within each of the above sectors, the author investigates the prospects for a number of developed nations. Very often there are some relations or correlations between the prospects of a country across the six sectors. If a country is anticipated to do well in one sector, it is often likely to do well in several other sectors as well.[citation needed][original research?]

For instance, across all sectors, he expects the US to fare relatively well. It has an extensive network of maritime transportation across very favorable waterways, including optimal access to the Atlantic and Pacific oceans. It has the deepest and best integrated capital markets. Because of the shale oil revolution, it has become increasingly independent regarding its energy needs. And, it has a large, dependably productive agricultural sector, being a major food exporter, due to a favorable climate and abundant fertile lands.[citation needed][original research?]

On the other hand, the author is less enthusiastic about the prospects for both China and Russia across several of the mentioned sectors. They both suffer from an aging demographic profile, less than optimal transportation waterways network, and their respective capital markets are not nearly as deep and integrated as the US (in part due to global sanctions against Russia, and a closed capital market in China). Additionally, China imports much of its petroleum and food requirements. In a deglobalized world, both countries will face major challenges on several fronts, according to the author.[citation needed][original research?]

Similarly, Europe will face several challenges of its own including ageing demographics, energy dependence vulnerability, and lack of access to domestic industrial raw materials. Africa and India will have numerous problems, including the most existential one, the ability to feed their citizens.[citation needed][original research?]1 / 1ChatGPT"The End of the World Is Just the Beginning" by Peter Zeihan delves into the forthcoming era of deglobalization, predicting a transition where nations will revert to greater self-reliance across crucial economic sectors. Drawing from his extensive research and experience in geopolitical intelligence, Zeihan analyzes the potential future of six economic sectors:AgricultureEnergyFinanceManufacturingMaterialsTransportZeihan identifies patterns of strength and vulnerability in different countries, often noting correlations across sectors. For instance, the U.S. is anticipated to perform well across all sectors due to its robust maritime transport system, integrated capital markets, energy independence from the shale oil revolution, and a robust agricultural sector. These advantages position the U.S. favorably in a deglobalizing world.Conversely, China and Russia are presented as facing numerous challenges in this impending reality. Aging populations, less efficient transport networks, and less developed capital markets are among the hurdles they will encounter. Specific external factors, like global sanctions against Russia and China's closed capital market, further exacerbate their predicament. Zeihan also points out China's dependency on imports for its energy and food needs.Europe, too, is anticipated to confront challenges in this deglobalized context. Aging populations, reliance on external energy sources, and a lack of indigenous industrial raw materials are among its potential vulnerabilities. Africa and India, meanwhile, grapple with even more fundamental challenges, notably ensuring food security for their vast populations.In essence, Zeihan's work offers a comprehensive overview of a world transitioning away from the globalization era, highlighting nations' assets and vulnerabilities in this changing landscape.1 / 1Analytical framework
Edit
Demography. The book examines age pyramids, a country's population aging over time and into the future. This gives him a view of a country's prospect for its labor force growth or contraction over time. In turn, this informs him on the overall economic prospects of a country in terms of economic growth, rising living standards, and other indices.
Geography. The book has a particular focus on access to oceans and internal waterways (rivers), as he considers that water transport is by far the cheapest (relative to air transport, rail transport, highway transport); and, therefore, such waterways can provide a material competitive advantage in economics[clarification needed] and trade, both domestic and international.
History. Since the end of the Second World War, the United States has supported a safe and secure maritime world trading system by patrolling the global seas with the world's most powerful navy. As the US commitment to safeguarding this maritime world trading system wanes, this has the potential to disrupt world trade. He expects the US to fare reasonably well in this deglobalized world, and most other countries and regions to not fare as well.[citation needed][original research?]1 / 1ChatGPTPeter Zeihan's "The End of the World Is Just the Beginning" employs a tripartite analytical framework, encompassing demography, geography, and history to provide a comprehensive understanding of the impending era of deglobalization.Demography: The book utilizes age pyramids to assess the trajectory of a country's population aging, both currently and predictively. This demographic examination helps Zeihan forecast potential labor force growth or contraction, which then offers insights into a country's future economic vitality. Key aspects like economic expansion, quality of life improvements, and other critical indicators are predicted based on these demographic trends.Geography: Zeihan emphasizes the importance of geographical attributes, specifically access to oceans and internal waterways. He posits that water-based transport (via oceans and rivers) is significantly more cost-effective compared to alternatives like air, rail, and road transport. Hence, nations with accessible waterways possess a distinct economic and trade advantage, both internally and internationally.History: The post-World War II era witnessed the U.S. establishing itself as the protector of global maritime trade, leveraging its powerful navy to ensure safe and unimpeded sea routes. Zeihan suggests that as the U.S. begins to retract from this role, global trade structures are likely to experience disruptions. In this potential new world order of reduced globalization, Zeihan anticipates that while the U.S. might navigate the challenges successfully, many other nations could face significant difficulties.By intersecting these three analytical pillars, Zeihan crafts a multifaceted perspective on the possible directions the world could take as the era of globalization winds down.1 / 1transport are largely over ... The implication is a potential market collapse for such products, as the globalized structures that enabled their wide distribution disintegrate.Manufacturing: The text suggests a bleak future for export-driven industries. Zeihan believes that mass-production assembly lines will become outdated. This hints at a shift away from economies of scale and perhaps towards more localized or specialized production methods. Furthermore, the pace of technological advancement in manufacturing might decelerate due to a blend of decreasing skilled labor availability (owing to demographic shifts) and a reduction in global networking. Without the seamless exchange of information that globalization enables, innovation might be stifled.Innovation & Product Cycles: Using the example of the iPhone, Zeihan highlights that even in optimistic scenarios, product innovation cycles will lengthen. This means that the rapid technological advancements and product releases consumers have become accustomed to may become less frequent.Demographic Challenges: The looming demographic decline, as painted by Zeihan, is compared to the impact of the Black Death in terms of its potential to reduce human populations. Such a massive decrease would significantly strain economies due to a shortage of workers, further complicating the challenges brought on by deglobalization.These excerpts underscore Zeihan's central thesis: the combined effects of deglobalization and demographic shifts will fundamentally transform the world economy, trade, and innovation in ways that are challenging and unprecedented.1 / 1before... Early life, education, and career
Edit
Zeihan was born in 1973,[4][5] and grew up as the adopted son of educators Jerald and Agnes Zeihan in Marshalltown, Iowa. He graduated from Marshalltown High School in 1992.[6][7] In 1995, he obtained a BSc in Political Science from what then was Northeast Missouri State University, and a postgraduate diploma in Asian studies from University of Otago (Dunedin, New Zealand) in 1997.

Discouraged by his experiences during his work at the American Embassy in Australia and at Susan Eisenhower's think tank, the Center for Political and Strategic Studies, he began working as an analyst for Austin-based geopolitical intelligence firm Stratfor in 2000.[7][8][9] Zeihan spent 12 years at Stratfor, eventually rising to vice-president.[9]

While still at Stratfor, Zeihan coauthored his first book, A Crucible of Nations, with Lauren Goodrich in 2011. The book discusses the Caucasus region of Eastern Europe.

Zeihan left Stratfor in 2012, founding his consulting firm Zeihan on Geopolitics that same year. His client list grew to include energy companies, financial institutions, business associations, agricultural interests, universities, and other government organizations.[10]

In 2014 he released Accidental Superpower. The book was reviewed by The Washington Post, The Wall Street Journal, and Kirkus Reviews.[8][11][12] The book focused on topographical and geographical landmarks (rivers, oceans, mountains, etc.) as distinct advantages in a state's ability to dominate other countries in economically, industrially, and militarily. With the use of maps, Zeihan pointed out that navigable rivers, or access to the oceans, along with a reliable road or rail network make a critical difference.[8] He subsequently published three more books The Absent Superpower (2017), Disunited Nations (2020), and The End of the World Is Just the Beginning (2022).1 / 1ChatGPTPeter Zeihan is an American geopolitical analyst and author, known for his work on global geopolitics and the potential impact of geography on countries' future prospects.Key Points:Personal Details:Born: January 18, 1973 (Age 50 as of the date given).Nationality: American.Early Life & Education:Born in 1973 and was adopted by educators Jerald and Agnes Zeihan in Marshalltown, Iowa.Graduated from Marshalltown High School in 1992.Earned a BSc in Political Science from Northeast Missouri State University in 1995.Obtained a postgraduate diploma in Asian studies from the University of Otago in New Zealand in 1997.Career:Worked at the American Embassy in Australia and at Susan Eisenhower's think tank, the Center for Political and Strategic Studies.Joined Austin-based geopolitical intelligence firm Stratfor in 2000 and served there for 12 years, eventually becoming vice-president.Co-authored his first book, "A Crucible of Nations," in 2011 while at Stratfor. This book explored the Caucasus region of Eastern Europe.Left Stratfor in 2012 and established his own consulting firm, Zeihan on Geopolitics. Zeihan underscores the importance of navigable waterways and reliable transportation networks in this dynamic.Subsequent publications include "The Absent Superpower" (2017), "Disunited Nations" (2020), and "The End of the World Is Just the Beginning" (2022).Zeihan's work reflects a unique blend of geopolitics with geography, emphasizing the tangible impact of a country's topographical features on its global influence and prosperity.1 / 1These articles were mostly written by a user named Sympa. Abstract 
I propose the âPropositional Accountâ of ef f ective quantum i eld theories. According 
to the Propositional Account, each ef f ective quantum i eld theory expresses proposi- 
tions about various physical items: i elds, interactions, and more.In addition, two 
ef f ective quantum i eld theories are physically equivalent just in case they express the 
same propositions. As I explain, the Propositional Account is scientif i cally naturalistic, 
since it invokes terms and principles from the empirical science of linguistics. And the 
Propositional Account avoids problems faced by other accounts of the physical contents 
of ef f ective theories. 
1Introduction 
What do ef f ective quantum i eld theories say about the physical world? And when are 
two ef f ective quantum i eld theories physically equivalent? What, in other words, are the 
physical contents of ef f ective theories, and when are two such theories physically the same? 
In this paper, I present an account of ef f ective quantum i eld theoriesâcall it the âPropo- 
sitional Accountââwhich answers these questions. As will become clear, there is much to like 
about the Propositional Account. It embodies a naturalistic approach to physical content, 
since it draws on the empirical science of linguistics. And it does not face problems that arise 
for other accounts of the contents of physical theories. 1

The article introduces the 'Propositional Account' for understanding effective quantum field theories. This account asserts that each effective quantum field theory expresses certain propositions about fields, interactions, etc. For two theories to be physically equivalent, they must express the same propositions. The Propositional Account is rooted in the empirical science of linguistics and it addresses challenges faced by other approaches in understanding the contents of effective theories.Introduction:
The paper aims to clarify what effective quantum field theories reveal about the physical world and to determine when two such theories can be considered as physically equivalent. The 'Propositional Account' provides answers to these queries. This account is appealing because it takes a naturalistic approach, drawing from linguistics, and doesn't encounter the issues that other accounts face when trying to define the contents of physical theories.Section 2 - Physical Content:

Feynman path integral, for instance, invokes an ill-def i ned measure over all trajectories. So no

Here is the third problem: Privileged Mappings does not respect the fact that the 
same mathematical structure can be used to represent physically distinct situations. To see 
why, suppose that the âcertain privileged mappingsâ, in Privileged Mappings, are taken to 
be isomorphisms of algebras, or dif f eomorphisms of manifolds, or something like that. Then 
Privileged Mappings implies that the relevant theories, corresponding to those algebras or

Just as the grammatical structures of two natural languages could be isomorphic, and yet 
the corresponding words in those languages could still have dif f erent meanings, the formal 
structures of two scientif i c theories could be isomorphic, and yet the corresponding terms in 
those theories could have dif f erent meanings as well. 
5Conclusion 
There is much to like about the Propositional Account. It provides an account of the 
physical contents of ef f ective theories. It provides an account of the conditions under which 
ef f ective theories are physically equivalent. It embodies a naturalistic approach to content. 
And it avoids problems that alternative accounts face. The Propositional Account is worth 
taking seriously. 
10Versions of this point are discussed in (Belot, 2013; Teitel, 2021).1 / 1ChatGPTSummary of the Continued Article "The Propositional Account of Effective Theories" by Isaac Wilhelm:Formal Techniques and Problems:
Many of the formal techniques that physicists use to deduce empirical predictions from effective theories are not rigorously defined in mathematical terms. For instance, the Feynman path integral makes use of a measure that isn't clearly defined over all trajectories. As such, no strictly defined mappings can align with the mathematically vague (yet physically meaningful) techniques physicists often employ. Therefore, when dealing with effective theories, the idea of 'privileged mappings' as favored by some philosophers falls short.Third Problem with Privileged Mappings:
A significant issue with the "Privileged Mappings" approach is that it doesn't consider the possibility that the same mathematical structure might describe different physical scenarios. For instance, should privileged mappings be understood as isomorphisms of algebras or diffeomorphisms of manifolds, then the related theories are seen as physically equivalent. However, this viewpoint is flawed since a single mathematical algebra could represent multiple distinct physical systems. Drawing a parallel with language, even if two languages have similar grammatical structures, words in each might have different meanings. Similarly, while two scientific theories might have analogous formal structures, the terms within those theories could differ in meaning.Conclusion:
The Propositional Account offers several advantages. It offers clarity on the content of effective theories and establishes criteria for determining the physical equivalence of these theories. Grounded in a naturalistic approach to content, the Propositional Account sidesteps the problems alternative methods face, making it a perspective worth serious consideration.1 / 1Can you give a simplified explanation?1 / 1ChatGPTCertainly!Simplified Summary:
Isaac Wilhelm proposes the "Propositional Account" for understanding effective quantum field theories. This approach says that these theories express specific statements or propositions about the physical world. Two theories are considered the same if they express the same propositions. This approach is different from and avoids the problems of another method called "Privileged Mappings." The latter method tried to use specific mathematical structures to describe physical situations but had problems because the same mathematical format could describe different physical scenarios. In conclusion, the "Propositional Account" is seen as a promising and more straightforward way to understand these quantum theories.1 / 1I don't think I understand it1 / 1ChatGPTNo worries! But this has issues. The same math can sometimes describe different things, causing confusion.New Way ("Propositional Account" by Isaac Wilhelm): Instead of just math, think of these theories as making clear statements about the universe. Two theories are the same if they say the same thing, even if the math looks different.Why is the New Way Good?: It's simpler, avoids the confusion of the old way, and is more in line with how scientists actually work.1 / 1corresponding to medium-sized dry goods. Similarly for ef f ective theories. A true ef f ective theory LÎexpresses facts like âThe

3Physical Equivalence 
In this section, I present the second principle of the Propositional Account. This prin- 
ciple describes physical equivalence among ef f ective theories. After presenting this principle, 
I defend itâand Physical Contentâagainst objections.And I argue for these principles 
by invoking a methodological criterion which accounts of physical content should generally 
satisfy. 
The physical equivalence principle is as follows; note that it implicitly invokes Physical 
Content. 
Physical Equivalence 
For each energy level Î, and for all ef f ective theories L1,Îand L2,Îat that energy level, 
L1,Îis physically equivalent to L2,Îif and only if L1,Îand L2,Îexpress exactly the 
same physical propositions. 
In other words, ef f ective theories are equivalent just in case the physical propositions they 
expressâas given by Physical Contentâare the same. 7 
https://doi.org/10.1017/psa.2023.117 Published online by Cambridge University Press 
Physical Content and Physical Equivalence jointly form what I have been calling the 
âPropositional Accountâ of ef f ective theories. Physical Content specif i es those theoriesâ phys- 
ical contents. Physical Equivalence uses those contents to state the conditions under which 
one ef f ective theory is physically equivalent to another. 
The Propositional Account implies that ef f ective theories are extremely i ne-grained. 
In particular, according to the Propositional Account, many empirically equivalent ef f ective 
theories are physically inequivalent. For many ef f ective theories make the same experimental 
predictions, and yet posit radically dif f erent i elds, interactions, and so on. Ef f ective theories 
formulated using canonical quantization, for instance, are physically dif f erent from ef f ective 
theories formulated using path integrals, even if these two classes of theories make the same 
empirical predictions: while the former theories posit i elds associating physical operator 
quantities with spacetime points, the latter theories posit i elds associating physical scalar 
quantities with spacetime points instead.

renormalized constants and a dif f erent renormalized Lagrangian density. The empirical pre-

5Conclusion 
There is much to like about the Propositional Account. It provides an account of the 
physical contents of ef f ective theories. It provides an account of the conditions under which 
ef f ective theories are physically equivalent. It embodies a naturalistic approach to content. 
And it avoids problems that alternative accounts face. The Propositional Account is worth 
taking seriously.1 / 1ChatGPTThis article delves into the philosophy of science, specifically regarding effective theories and their content and equivalence. accounts of the contents of physical theories. 
Content Naturalism Criterion 
Philosophical accounts of content should generally be formulated using the theoretical

Here's a brief overview of both:Church-Turing thesis:The Church-Turing thesis postulates that everything "computable" can be computed by a Turing machine. This means that if there's an algorithmic way to determine the outcome of a problem, then there's a Turing machine that can determine that outcome.It's not a formal theorem that can be proven within a particular theoretical model, but it's a foundational principle in computer science.Named after Alonzo Church and Alan Turing, who independently proposed this notion around the same time.Curry-Howard isomorphism (also known as the Curry-Howard correspondence or the proofs-as-programs and propositions-as-types principle):It establishes a direct correspondence between formal proofs in logic and programs in computation.Specifically, it notes that there's a relationship between systems of formal logic as used in proof theory and computational calculi used in type theory.For instance, under this correspondence:Propositions (statements that can be true or false) correspond to types in a type system.Proofs of these propositions correspond to values (or programs) of those types.Named after Haskell Curry and William Howard, who noted these correspondences.Relation:
The Church-Turing thesis and the Curry-Howard isomorphism, though dealing with different aspects of the computational landscape, together emphasize the deep connections between computation, logic, and mathematics. While the Church-Turing thesis gives us a broad definition of what's computable, the Curry-Howard isomorphism bridges the world of mathematical logic with that of computation, suggesting that the act of proving mathematical theorems and the act of computing can be viewed through the same lens. This has profound implications for fields like type theory, functional programming, and more.1 / 1I mean connections with the positional account and privileged mapping.1 / 1ChatGPTAh, I see. In contrast, asynchronous circuits do not have a global clock; they progress based on the data's readiness. There have been challenges in designing complex asynchronous circuits because of the lack of a global synchronizing mechanism.Null Convention Logic (NCL) is a technique used to design asynchronous circuits. It employs a dual-rail encoding system where every bit of information has two lines representing it. The use of propagating null wavefronts helps ensure that each computation is completed and acknowledged before the next one begins. This approach ensures that all potential hazards (like race conditions) are handled.When you introduce tristate buffers and use NCL, you can create a representation where the distinction between synchronous and asynchronous circuits becomes blurred. Essentially, the synchronous paradigm's structured, clock-driven behavior can be mapped into the asynchronous paradigm's data-driven behavior.This equivalence opens the door for potential benefits from both worlds. From the asynchronous side, you can have lower power consumption and potentially faster operations since you don't need to wait for a clock cycle if the data is ready sooner. From the synchronous side, designers can leverage established design and verification methodologies.It's a compelling direction in digital circuit design, highlighting the innovative ways in which researchers and engineers are trying to harness the advantages of both synchronous and asynchronous designs.1 / 1Here's a poem I wrote about null convention logic and process invocation:

the name forming values. If the name forming values are called âdataâ values 
the newly assigned value will be a ânot dataâ value called NULL. A name 
formed of âdataâ values will express âa data name.â A name formed of all 
NULL values will express ânot a data name.â A data name and all NULL can 
form alternately in relation to each other as shown in Figure 5.9. The formation 
of each name is a discrete appearance event in its value domain. A data name 
can form in relation to all NULL. And all NULL can form in relation to a data 
name. In both cases the discrete completeness of name formation (all NULL 
or complete data) can be directly appreciated by the value transform rules. 
These monotonic transitionings will be called wavefronts. The monotonic 
transition from âcompletely NULLâ to âcompletely dataâ is a data wavefront 
and the transition from âcompletely dataâ to âcompletely NULLâ is a NULL 
wavefront. Successive âdataâ names are separated by an all NULL ânot dataâ 
name. This will be referred to as the NULL convention. 
The Completeness Criterion Each operator must now appreciate these 
completeness relations in terms of its value transform rules. Each operator 
must transition its asserted value only when its input values are a completely 
formed data name or are all NULL. The following three rules condition the 
behavior of an operator: 
â¢ If input is âcompletely data,â then transition output to the âdataâ resolu- 
tion of input. 
â¢ If input is âcompletely NULL,â then transition output to âNULLâ. 
â¢ If input is neither âcompletely dataâ nor âcompletely NULL,â do not 
transition output. 
The transition of the output to a data value implies the completeness of 
data presentation at the input, the completeness of its resolution and that the

a NULL Convention Logic.

NULL Convention Logic introduces a third value: NULL. Think of NULL as a "no data" or "undefined" state, different from 0 or 1.The NULL Convention:If all values are 'data' (either 0 or 1), it's called a "data name."If all values are NULL, it's called a "not a data name."These states change in relation to each other, moving from a complete set of data values to all NULL values and vice versa. These transitions are termed "wavefronts."A "data wavefront" transitions from all NULL to all data. A "NULL wavefront" transitions from all data to all NULL.The Completeness Criterion:An operator (like an AND gate or an OR gate in circuits) should only change its output based on completely formed inputs.If all inputs are data, the operator produces a data output.If all inputs are NULL, the operator produces a NULL output.If the inputs are a mix of data and NULL, the operator doesn't change its output.Enhanced Boolean Functions:In NCL, Boolean functions (like AND, OR, NOT) have a "completeness behavior". This means they respond to data and NULL inputs in a way that holds their state or output until the inputs are completely data or completely NULL.This creates a coordination in the system where every component waits for complete information before proceeding, making the whole system synchronized.The main idea behind NULL Convention Logic is to provide a coordinated and predictable behavior in circuits. 2.8 CONCLUSION 
With the traditional mathematical notion of expressing a process in terms 
of composing functions, the behavior of the mathematician with a pencil em- 
bodies a critical expressivity of the behavior of the process. The mathemati- 
cian knows when data is ready to be presented to the next function and when 
to write down each function and substitute its data. If the mathematician is 
not available, this expressivity of behavior is lost, and on their own, the behav- 
ior of composed functions becomes indeterminate. The lost expression of 
behavior embodied in the missing mathematician must be restored to the 
behaving functions. 
The expression of the mathematicianâs behavior can be restored in two 
ways. One way is to retain the notion of a mathematical function as a primitive 
form and add other forms of expression such as time intervals, memory, and 
explicit control properly coordinated with the expression of the functions. The 
other way is to enhance the symbolic expression of the functions and the data 
to include the necessary expression of coordination behavior. 
2.8.1 A Question of Primitivity 
If one retains the notion of the mathematical function then one is confronted 
with the fact that a composition of functions do not work properly and will 
assert a rash of incorrect results before settling to an assertion of a correct 
result. If one adopts the notion of the enhanced functions, a composition of 
enhanced functions work properly and transition to a correct result without 
any assertion of incorrect results. 
The incorrect behavior of a composition of mathematical functions can be 
isolated by associating a time interval with the expression. By analyzing the 
delay behavior of the components and their composite delay behavior for a 
specif i c implementation, a time interval can be def i ned for that specif i c imple- 
mentation that extends from presentation of input to beyond the incorrect 
behavior into the period of stable correct behavior. The interval can control 
a memory associated with the expression output of the expression to sample 
the correct result. The indeterminate logical behavior is thus isolated by the 
time interval and the memory. The expression is now in terms of logic, memory 
and time. The time behavior and the logical behavior have to be properly 
coordinated for the expression to work correctly. 
A composition of enhanced functions does not assert incorrect behavior 
and there is no need to isolate its logical behavior. It remains purely in terms 
of logical behavior. 
The logic expression of the mathematical functions, the memory and the 
time interval form a unit of expression that can be further composed in terms

of shared memories and shared time intervals. The shared time intervals must 
be all be identical and in phase. This greater composition is a structure of 
expressions behaving synchronously in relation to a common time interval: a 
clock. 
An expression of enhanced functions can logically regulate its input with 
its own completeness behavior and a feedback path from its output to its input 
forming a cycle. Further composition occurs in terms of interlinked cycles. The 
greater composition is a structure of cycles each behaving purely in terms of 
logical relationships and the composition as a whole behaving purely in terms 
of logical relationships. It is a fully deterministic expression of distributed 
concurrent behavior. 
The clock coordinating the behavior of the mathematical functions isolates 
all logical relationships. The logical relationships of the expression are not 
available and have to be reconstituted in terms of a new logical expression of 
explicit control. The clocked greater composition performs one set of behaviors 
every interval tick. The new level of explicit control can only compose in terms 
of a sequence of interval tick behaviors. The incompetence of the mathematical 
functions has led to explicitly controlled, strictly sequential behavior. 
At some point the greater expression of enhanced functions will be reused 
iteratively. Continued composition might occur sequentially but it need not. 
The logical behaviors of the expression were never isolated so its complete 
logical structure is intact and available. This logical structure can be parti- 
tioned in various ways to allow parallel and pipeline iterative behaviors. 
Mathematical functions do not behave properly to begin with. In correcting 
the behavior of the functions, one is led through a progression of supporting 
concepts to sequentiality. The coordinating behavior of the mathematician is 
only partially restored with a complex scaffolding of concepts. Enhanced func- 
tions work properly to begin, require no additional supporting concepts, and 
leads to distributed concurrency. The coordination behavior of the mathema- 
tician is fully restored with a single simple conceptual reorientation. 
2.8.2 A Labyrinth of Concepts 
Mathematical functions do not work. The concepts necessary to make them 
work leads to an ad hoc scaffolding of mutually supporting concepts that is 
diff i cult to escape: stateless mathematical function, 
time interval, 
synchronicity, 
sequentiality, 
explicit control, 
common memory, and 
extended state space.

With the NULL convention and the enhanced functions the expression of

2.7 THE COMPLEXITY OF SEQUENTIALITY 
Glimpsing the simplicity of concurrency reveals the inherent complexity of 
sequentiality. 
2.7.1 Unavoidable Concurrency 
A sequence is a mapping from a concurrent; partially ordered expression. It 
cannot be any other way. The partially ordering of the fl ow of data among the 
functions is simple and direct, and expresses the necessary and inherent struc- 
ture of a process. Understanding and expressing the partial ordering cannot 
be avoided. 
A programmer typically starts a programming task by scribbling fl ow graphs 
in a notebook. The programmer then translates these partially ordered graphs 
into a sequence of operations. Getting the sequence right is not the important 
thing. The important thing is getting the partial ordering relationships right 
within the sequence. The partial ordering of the dependency relationships is 
the referent for the correctness of a sequence. There are many possible correct 
sequences that express a given process and every one of them must conform 
to the same partial ordering: the same expression of concurrency.1 / 1ChatGPTThis text seems to be discussing the inherent relationship between concurrency and sequentiality in the realm of computational processes and their design. Let's break down the main ideas presented:Partitioning Network of Functions:Functions can be grouped into different layers or sections based on their implementation (hardware, firmware, software) and their coordination protocols.They can also be organized laterally into coupled cycles (for pipeline structures) or into multi-threaded sequences.NULL Convention and Enhanced Functions:These techniques make expressing concurrent behaviors as simple as expressing strictly sequential behaviors. This raises a question about the actual simplicity of sequential behaviors.Complexity of Sequentiality:By observing the simplicity with which concurrent processes can be expressed, we start to see the inherent complexity in sequential processes.Unavoidable Concurrency:Sequences are derived from concurrently arranged, partially ordered expressions.This partial ordering is a simple and direct representation of how data flows among functions. It's the inherent structure of any process.Expressing and understanding this partial ordering is unavoidable.From Flow Graphs to Sequences:Programmers often start by sketching flow graphs, which depict the partial orderings of function executions or data flow.These flow graphs are then translated into sequences of operations. The crux isn't just to get the sequence right but to ensure that the partial ordering relationships are accurate within that sequence.The real reference for sequence correctness is this partial ordering of dependency relationships. There could be multiple correct sequences for a single process, but they all must adhere to the same inherent concurrent structure or partial ordering.In essence, the text argues that even in what we consider to be "strictly sequential" processes, there's an underlying concurrent structure that guides the order and flow of operations. Let's unpack this a bit:Traditionally, in both education and practice, sequentiality has been the foundation of computer science. Algorithms, as taught in traditional computer science courses, are essentially step-by-step procedures or formulas for solving problems, which emphasize a sequential approach. However, as computing evolved, particularly with the rise of parallel processing and distributed systems, it became clear that purely sequential models don't capture the complexity or potential of modern computing systems.Karl Fant, in "Computer Science Reconsidered," seems to argue against the notion of sequentiality as the primary or "primitive" mode of computation. Instead, he advocates for viewing computation in terms of concurrent behaviors, where multiple processes or functions can operate simultaneously, interacting with each other in a coordinated manner. This notion aligns more closely with how many modern computer systems operate, especially given the ubiquity of multi-core processors and distributed architectures.The "invocation model of process expression" seems to be a proposed framework by Fant that emphasizes this concurrent behavior, drawing parallels with how biological systems like cells function. In this model, computations (akin to functions) are invoked based on their interactions with other computations, rather than following a strict, predetermined sequence. This offers a more dynamic, adaptive, and potentially efficient approach to computation.Fant's perspective is a challenge to traditional computational thinking and underscores the importance of evolving our foundational concepts to better align with modern computational realities.1 / 1It also seems he has an interesting perspective on the role computer science, which he argues which is to eliminate the need for the human to provide symbolic intervention. 1 / 1ChatGPTThis perspective emphasizes the automation potential of computer science and resonates with its broader goals: to automate processes, reason about information, and manage complexity in such a way that humans don't need to intervene at every step.By arguing for the elimination of the need for human symbolic intervention, Fant seems to suggest that well-designed computer systems should be able to manage and process information based on the inherent logic and rules encoded within them, without requiring constant human guidance. Early computers required extensive human intervention for even simple tasks, whereas modern systems, driven by sophisticated algorithms and AI, can handle complex tasks with minimal human input.This perspective also ties back to his emphasis on concurrency over sequentiality. In a system that operates based on sequential logic, there's often a need for human intervention to manage exceptions, handle unexpected inputs, or guide processes. In contrast, a system designed with concurrency and adaptability in mind can potentially manage these challenges autonomously.Fant's viewpoint underscores the idea that computer science isn't just about creating tools that execute human commands, but about designing systems that can autonomously reason, adapt, and operate based on the principles and rules embedded within them. COMPUTER SCIENCE 
Humans have always been integral to the works of mathematics. Mathemati- 
cians devise symbol systems, including algorithms, to manipulate the symbols. 
They then enliven the symbol system by manipulating its symbols on paper 
according to the rules of an algorithm. While the manipulating human has been 
eliminated and replaced with a machine, the humans that conceive symbol 
systems and the humans that engineer the manipulating machines remain in 
the works. However, it is possible to eliminate these humans as well. 
3.1 THE HUMANS IN COMPUTER SCIENCE 
Today computer science with its mathematical heritage retains humans in the 
works. These humans constitute an element of arbitrarily suff i cient expressiv- 
ity. If one is only interested in the nature of a symbol system independent of 
how it might be expressed, then any workable expression of a symbol system 
will suff i ce. Although appeal to arbitrarily suff i cient expressivity can be con- 
veniently effective, if one is seeking insight into the nature of expression itself, 
the presence of arbitrarily suff i cient expressivity fundamentally undermines 
the effort. 
If there is an arbitrarily suff i cient interstitial mortar, then the conceptual 
bricks do not have to fi t well. Any concepts can be cobbled together into an 
apparently universal whole that is adequately functional and that can even 
appear to be simple in some compelling sense. But the element of arbitrary

suff i ciency eliminates the necessity of the concepts fi tting together and pre- 
cludes the possibility of discovering appropriate concepts and how they might 
fi t. A fudged model cannot provide insightful understanding or unifying con- 
nections. Appeal to arbitrary suff i ciency can reveal nothing about essential 
necessity. 
Saying a human does it in computer science is like saying a god does it in 
physics. The humans in the works both enable the computer and deny it theo- 
retical closure. This diff i culty of humans in the works is explicitly recognized 
in the view of the computer as an artifact and the acceptance that computers 
cannot be theorized about in the same sense that natural phenomena can be 
theorized about [2]. 
âIf what the computer scientist says about computers in theory does not 
agree with behavior, he or she can always change the computerâ to match the 
theory [1]. 
The essential problem is that there is no way to compare conceptual models. 
The humans in the works ensure that all models, even those with partially 
characterizing or misleading concepts, will appear equally successful. There is 
no criterion of failure, no hint of inadequacy. With the inability to theorize 
the only approach to understanding the subject appears to be experience and 
experiment, and the only approach to managing it appears to be imposed 
rationale and convention. Imposing mathematical rationale and convention 
seems reasonable and convenient. 
But are computers and symbol systems as artifactual as supposed? Are 
humans necessary to symbol systems. Symbolic computing mechanisms exist 
in nature, particularly in biology. Computer science aspires to encompass 
these symbol systems. A conceptual model of natureâs symbol systems cannot
have humans in the works. Can a conceptual model of symbolic expression be 
conceived that does not require humans? 
3.2 ELIMINATING THE HUMANS 
It has long been recognized that the symbol-manipulating human might be 
replaced by a machine. The development of computer science to date is all 
about replacing the manipulating human in the works with a spontaneously 
behaving machine: the computer. But there are still humans involved in the 
conception of the symbol system and in the design of the mechanism. These 
humans are somewhat more diff i cult to remove. 
3.2.1 The Engineering Human 
The diff i culty with removing the engineering human is that the manipulating 
human was not completely eliminated to begin with. The manipulating human

provided something more than just the enlivenment of the symbolic expres- 
sions. The human also provided coordination behavior. Symbolic expressions 
do not include the expression of coordinating behavior. So simply enlivening 
a symbolic expression with spontaneously behaving symbols and their interac- 
tions is not suff i cient. Coordination behavior must also be added to the en- 
livened expression, and this is added by a human engineer. The diff i culty is 
illustrated with a Boolean expression of a full adder expressed in terms of two 
half adders shown in Figure 3.1. 
The Boolean logic expression can be enlivened by mapping the symbolic 
expression to spontaneously behaving symbols and spontaneously behaving 
symbol interactions (functions). When a new input state is presented to the 
inputs of the Boolean combinational expression, a stable wavefront of correct 
result values fl ows from the input through the network of functions to the 
output. But since Boolean functions are continuously responsive and since 
some functions and signal paths can be faster than others, invalid and indeter- 
minate result values may speed ahead of the stable wavefront of valid results. 
This rushing wavefront of indeterminacy may cause the output of the Boolean 
expression to transition through a large number of incorrect values before the 
stable wavefront of correct result values reaches the output and the expression 
as a whole stabilizes to the correct resolution of the presented input. The 
behavior of the enlivened symbolic expression is not determinate. 
This indeterminate behavior does not occur when the manipulating human 
with a pencil enlivens the expression. The human can determine when all the 
input symbols are available for each function and resolve each function in its 
proper turn. The resolution of the expression fl ows to completion with no 
ambiguity of behavior. 
There is no way to determine, solely in terms of the behavior of the enliv- 
ened expression itself, when the stable wavefront of correct results reaches 
the output. However, an enlivened expression can be relied on to eventually 
stabilize to a correct result state. After presentation of an input, it is suff i cient 
to wait an appropriate time interval, characterized by the slowest propagation 
path through the expression, to ensure that the wavefront of stable result 
values has propagated through the expression and that the output of the 
expression has stabilized to the correct resolution of the presented input. This 
time interval, however, is not symbolic, is implementation specif i c, and cannot 
be derived from the symbolic expression. It requires the participation of an 
engineering human.

The arbitrarily expressive engineering human in the works contrives to 
make the insuff i ciently expressive enlivened Boolean expressions work. If a 
Boolean logic expression cannot behave correctly on its own without the 
assistance of a human, it must be considered a conceptual failure. This circum- 
stance can be viewed in two ways. One can assign theoretical primacy to 
Boolean logic anyway and regard this circumstance as showing that humans 
are necessary and cannot be eliminated from the works of symbolic expres- 
sion. Or one can search for a model that works on its own symbolic terms 
without human assistance. 
3.2.2 Eliminating the Human Engineer 
The Boolean logic expression of the full-adder can be symbolically expressed 
in a different way. The Boolean logic expression uses two unique symbols, 0 
and 1, and unique places within the expression to represent different meanings 
within the expression. Each unique meaning is expressed as a combination of 
symbol and place (wire). The 0 or 1 on one wire is different from the 0 or 1 
on a different wire. These unique place-value meanings of the Boolean logic 
expression can be mapped into an expression purely in terms of unique 
symbols. 
Imagine that there are a multitude of unique symbols available such that 
each unique meaning can be represented by a unique symbol. Such a mapping 
of unique symbols to meanings is shown in relation to the Boolean circuit in 
Figure 3.2. Two unique symbols for each wire in the circuit represent the 0 
value and the 1 value for that wire. 
C means X = 0 
D means X = 1 
E means Y = 0 
F means Y = 1 and so on for each wire in the circuit. 
Next imagine a set of rules that express how the symbols interact and trans- 
form into other symbols such as the set of rules below. GI[S] means the com- 
bination of symbols G and I transform into the symbol S. The interaction rules 
for the behavior of each logic operator are derived from the symbols associ- 
ated with each operator and its particular logical operation.1 / 1ChatGPTFant's perspective on computer science here is quite philosophical, diving deep into the foundational elements of the field. The discussion touches on the following key points:Humans in Computer Science: The text begins by addressing the human role in computer science. Historically, humans have been deeply embedded in mathematical and computational processes. Even with the introduction of automated computers, humans still play roles in conceiving the symbolic systems and engineering the machines that execute them.Arbitrary Sufficient Expressivity: The argument here is about the limitations of having "humans in the works." Such systems, though functional, might not reflect the inherent necessities of computation.Limitations of Current Symbol Systems: Fant highlights the shortcomings of certain symbolic representations, like Boolean expressions, in reflecting the actual, autonomous behavior of computational systems. In contrast, when a human evaluates the same expression step by step, they inherently ensure proper coordination, resulting in deterministic behavior.Eliminating the Human Engineer: The discussion then shifts to a proposal of an alternative symbolic representation. Instead of the traditional binary (0 and 1) representation, Fant imagines a system where unique meanings are represented by unique symbols. This is a conceptual shift that moves away from place-value representations (where the meaning of a symbol can change based on its position) to a system where every unique meaning has its own distinct symbol. Such a system might have inherent properties that allow for more deterministic, human-independent execution.In essence, Fant is discussing the limitations of current symbolic systems and our reliance on humans to fill in the gaps. He suggests that a deeper understanding and a shift in representation might allow for truly autonomous computational systems. The effects of sweatshops are complex and have been widely debated. Here are some key aspects to consider:Negative Effects:Exploitation: Workers in sweatshops often face exploitation, including extremely low wages that are insufficient to cover basic living expenses. They may work long hours, sometimes in hazardous conditions, without appropriate safety measures.Poor Working Conditions: Sweatshops can have overcrowded, unsafe, and unsanitary working environments. The debate surrounding sweatshops revolves around ethical and moral questions. Some argue that sweatshops exploit vulnerable workers and should be abolished, while others contend that they provide opportunities for impoverished individuals and contribute to economic development.Efforts to address the negative effects of sweatshops include improving labor conditions, raising wages, enforcing labor laws, and promoting responsible business practices in global supply chains. Ethical consumerism, where consumers choose products from companies committed to fair labor practices, can also be a driving force for change.In conclusion, the effects of sweatshops are multifaceted, and the debate surrounding them continues. The previous two chapters discussed how expressional primitives associate 
and collaborate to express a greater stride of appreciation that recognizes and 
appreciates more differentness than any individual primitive could recognize. 
A pure value expression with a set of value transform rules can recognize and 
appreciate larger and more numerous formed names than any individual value 
transform rule. A structure of associated operators can recognize and appreci- 
ate larger and more numerous formed names than any individual operator. 
These greater expressions form behavior boundaries with their appreciation 
behavior. There is an input boundary that receives a presented name to appre- 
ciate, and there is an output boundary through which appreciation behavior 
is asserted. These greater expressions can be further composed into even 
greater expressions with greater strides of appreciation of differentness by 
associating output boundaries to input boundaries. 
This chapter discusses the composition of behavior boundaries to express 
a greater stride of appreciation. The discussion will be initially in terms of 
association expression. There can also be boundary relationships within a pure 
value expression that will be discussed.

7.1.1 Association Boundaries 
Consider the binary full-adder of Figure 7.1 that takes three binary inputs and 
asserts two binary outputs. The full-adder is bounded by inputs CI, X, and Y 
and outputs S and CO. 
Consider that the full-adder is composed of two three input expressions, S 
and C as in Figure 7.2. S outputs the sum and C outputs the carry. Each expres- 
sion has its own input and output boundary. If S and C express the complete- 
ness criterion, then their boundaries compose to express the completeness 
criterion for the full-adder. 
Consider that three input expressions are not available but only two input 
expressions are available. Figure 7.3 shows the full-adder in terms of two input 
NULL convention Boolean functions. Each function is bounded and expresses 
the completeness criterion. Again, the completeness relations of the boundar- 
ies of the functions accumulate so that the full-adder input and output bound- 
aries are completeness boundaries. The boundary of the full-adder encompasses 
the boundaries of the functions and appreciates a greater range of different- 
ness than any function individually.
